<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17576533475662849721">With the laugh-out-loud humor and heartfelt wisdom that made <strong>Animal Husbandry</strong> a national bestseller, Laura Zigman's second novel introduces Ellen Franck, a successful single career woman whose one desire--a child of her own--throws her into the ever-growing ranks of the "reproductively challenged."<br /><br />Ellen has a life many people dream about--a glamorous fashion industry job,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17576533475662849721">With the laugh-out-loud humor and heartfelt wisdom that made <strong>Animal Husbandry</strong> a national bestseller, Laura Zigman's second novel introduces Ellen Franck, a successful single career woman whose one desire--a child of her own--throws her into the ever-growing ranks of the "reproductively challenged."<br /><br />Ellen has a life many people dream about--a glamorous fashion industry job, an apartment in Greenwich Village, good friends--and yet Ellen feels herself at sixes and sevens, filled with a vague longing for...what? She can't say. Then the sight of her newborn niece, Nicole (a.k.a. "The Pickle"), makes her realize exactly what she's been missing: a child. But there's one problem. Malcolm, the man she loves, is too scarred by the long-ago death of his young son to ever consider fatherhood again.<br /><br />Looking down the barrel of the dark side of thirty-five, Ellen knows that time is passing, and as it does, her desire to have a baby only increases--especially when her sister Lynn announces she's pregnant with her second child. Now Ellen must finally address the very real flaws in her relationship with Malcolm and examine her doubts and fears about the only option that seems to be available--single motherhood. And so begins nine months of reading, Internet surfing, and nonstop Zigmanesque observations about morning sickness, stretch marks, accelerated hair growth, digestion, amniocentesis (and that's just the beginning). And Ellen...well, Ellen finally makes a clear-eyed decision that will change her life.<br /><br />This book has not been prepared, approved, or licensed by any entity that created or produced <em>Sesame Street.</em><br /><br /><br />Her biological clock ticking, Ellen's desire to have a baby only increases--especially when her sister Janice announces she's pregnant with her second child. Now Ellen must deal with the very real flaws in her relationship with Malcolm, and finally examine her doubts and fears about the only option that seems to be available--single motherhood. And so begins nine months of reading, Internet-surfing, and non-stop Zigmanesque observations about morning sickness, stretch marks, accelerated hair growth, digestion, amniocentesis (and that's just the beginning). And Ellen . . . well, Ellen makes a final clear-eyed decision that will change her life. --&gt;</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17576533475662849721">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_371637466">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/371637466" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11067136-amy" class="left imgcol" title="Amy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1447168865p2/11067136.jpg" alt="Amy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/371637466?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 08, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11067136-amy" class="user" title="Amy">Amy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/136268.Dating_Big_Bird" title="Paperback 9780385333412" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11067136-amy?shelf=just-plain-sucked" class="actionLinkLite">just-plain-sucked</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer371637466">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13406305487797034653">In a sweet nutshell, this book is horrible.<br /><br />The story focuses on Ellen, a flippy drippy bore with completely fucking warped perceptions of motherhood.<br /><br />Ellen is 35, lives in New York, works for a designer as a Marketing Exec and wants to have a baby. That's it. She seems to want NOTHING else out of her life! She hates her job, her boyfriend is an impotent car wreck of a human being (so head's up, if you're looking for sex in this book, it ain't happenin')!! The only thing she seems to care about, i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13406305487797034653">In a sweet nutshell, this book is horrible.<br /><br />The story focuses on Ellen, a flippy drippy bore with completely fucking warped perceptions of motherhood.<br /><br />Ellen is 35, lives in New York, works for a designer as a Marketing Exec and wants to have a baby. That's it. She seems to want NOTHING else out of her life! She hates her job, her boyfriend is an impotent car wreck of a human being (so head's up, if you're looking for sex in this book, it ain't happenin')!! The only thing she seems to care about, is her 4 year old diapered niece "Pickle". Yes, she calls the kid pickle! I'll get to THAT irritating shit in a minute.<br /><br />I think the most disappointing thing about this book is that Ellen is the most unlikable character! She's the kind of girl I would cross the street to avoid. When she's not focused on how fat everyone else is (all mothers by the way, catty bitch) she's hating them for being able to have a baby! Her life means nothing to her unless she can have a baby. What century are we in??? <br />Plus, she doesn't even seem to care that her boyfriend won't fuck her!! I mean, I see that the author is trying to make her all sensitive and such and that their relationship means more than sex (blah blah blah), but seriously any other woman would be going out of her mind!!! Ellen just sort of mentions it at times, like he keeps forgetting to bring milk home. Seriously?<br />Um, also, if you're desperate to have a baby you kind of need a man with a working penis!!<br /><br />And now the "Pickle". I'm sure she's cute and all, but has anyone realized this four year old is still in pampers??? The over the top sticky sweet moments between her and her niece were enough to make me gag. She even found her pitching a fit and screaming at the top of her lungs adorable. Who does that?<br /><br />Maybe I'm just not as sensitive to "motherly" desires, but as a 35 year single woman myself, I'm pretty happy with my career, family and social standing. What this woman is dying for, I just can't relate to!<br />I mean the writing itself isn't bad, I just found the characters so empty, whiny and annoying. Sorry, but two thumbs down for me.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13406305487797034653">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/23925803-raina-tellado" class="left imgcol" title="Raina Tellado"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1400195247p2/23925803.jpg" alt="Raina Tellado" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1150640414?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 06, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/23925803-raina-tellado" class="user" title="Raina Tellado">Raina Tellado</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/136268.Dating_Big_Bird" title="Paperback 9780385333412" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1150640414">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17786579956904997595">I think the reason that this book was so extremely disappointing was because I expected the story line to be about someone who actually dates Big Bird. What I really read was an annoying story about a woman who just wants to get pregnant. Not only was it cheesy and predictable and so far away from being my kind of a book, but I found some of the remarks to be offensive. "fag" and "retarded" were used surprisingly often and I got pissed, not gonna lie. This was just an annoying piece to read and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17786579956904997595">I think the reason that this book was so extremely disappointing was because I expected the story line to be about someone who actually dates Big Bird. What I really read was an annoying story about a woman who just wants to get pregnant. Not only was it cheesy and predictable and so far away from being my kind of a book, but I found some of the remarks to be offensive. "fag" and "retarded" were used surprisingly often and I got pissed, not gonna lie. This was just an annoying piece to read and I can't wait to move onto something different and get back into my genres of literature. I don't recommend this to anyone. </span>

Still, the world Zigman created and the characters within pulled me along to the ending. </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14793451972855440760">I loved this!<br /><br />I enjoyed every page of it and it got me constantly laughing.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText16881317144767127055">This book offers insight into a very real conflict among modern women, who struggle to balance finding a man, building a successful career, and raising a child (or children). While there were parts of this book that were humorous and relatable, I could not connect with the main character, who was desperate to have a child in order to become happy. Interestingly enough, along the way she also falls in love and becomes rich/famous, so it is impossible to say whether said baby actually improved her life or "having it all" was responsible. In either instance, this seemed to be too much like a fairy tale for me to appreciate. </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1117827027">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7094909671023670149">I am not, on the whole, a big fan of the chick lit genre. Oftentimes, I feel like if you've read one book of this ilk, you've read them all.<br /><br />But this book was a pleasant surprise. Ellen actually felt like a real person, and her relationships - with Amy, with her sister and mother, with Karen - actually felt believable. I found myself getting very invested in the story and in Ellen's struggle with the idea of having a child on her own.<br /><br />And while I wish the epilogue had been developed into a much la</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7094909671023670149">I am not, on the whole, a big fan of the chick lit genre. Oftentimes, I feel like if you've read one book of this ilk, you've read them all.<br /><br />But this book was a pleasant surprise. Ellen actually felt like a real person, and her relationships - with Amy, with her sister and mother, with Karen - actually felt believable. I found myself getting very invested in the story and in Ellen's struggle with the idea of having a child on her own.<br /><br />And while I wish the epilogue had been developed into a much larger part of the book, I was satisfied by the ending.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/19421489-susan-bazzett-griffith" class="user" title="Susan Bazzett-griffith">Susan Bazzett-griffith</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/136268.Dating_Big_Bird" title="Paperback 9780385333412" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/19421489-susan-bazzett-griffith?shelf=fun-chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">fun-chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer679557424">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer777866831999719412">An interesting and less-stereotypical-than-usual take on the chick lit/ mommy-lit genre. Zigman's Dating Big Bird is surprisingly mature for a book of it's ilk. Her protagonist, a single career woman in her mid-thirties, wants a child, dotes on her niece, and finds a friend in a similar situation. She actually shows the character realizing and ruminating on her decision to have a child on her own throughout the entire book, rather than the normal go-go-go pace of these types of books. She consid</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText777866831999719412">An interesting and less-stereotypical-than-usual take on the chick lit/ mommy-lit genre. Zigman's Dating Big Bird is surprisingly mature for a book of it's ilk. Her protagonist, a single career woman in her mid-thirties, wants a child, dotes on her niece, and finds a friend in a similar situation. She actually shows the character realizing and ruminating on her decision to have a child on her own throughout the entire book, rather than the normal go-go-go pace of these types of books. She considers all options, she continues to live her life, working, being an active member of her extended family, and listening to/considering all of the thoughts and advice of all the people around her. The book has characters representing all different kinds of mothers, and Zigman refuses to show any sort of favoritism to any of the characters' choices, which was refreshing. <br /><br />The reason I only give this book three stars is that, perhaps because of her careful handling of the subject matter, it was a little slow, and because the ending was more than a bit unbelievable. Honestly, this book screams- make a romantic comedy! Make this into a chick flick! And I didn't love that aspect of it at all and felt it took away from what could have been a more feminist-leaning/ empowering story. Dating Big Bird is a good read, though, for those who are into these kinds of books. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="777866831999719412">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer14554411">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3089483128269198310">Having three kids, I can fully relate to Ellen's (the main character who wants to be pregnant and have a child but has no way of getting pregnant) desire to have children. Those of us with kids will get a laugh out of the silly things she does while trying to decide whether to get pregnant and how to get pregnant. Not to mention the who. The whole working mother vs. stay at home mother delimna is really into play, and although it doesn't go into depth about which is "better" (although I don't se</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3089483128269198310">Having three kids, I can fully relate to Ellen's (the main character who wants to be pregnant and have a child but has no way of getting pregnant) desire to have children. Those of us with kids will get a laugh out of the silly things she does while trying to decide whether to get pregnant and how to get pregnant. Not to mention the who. The whole working mother vs. stay at home mother delimna is really into play, and although it doesn't go into depth about which is "better" (although I don't see either as being "better" than the other, just different from each other), it does bring up the hot topic. I'm not sure I really liked the end and the last 50-75 pages seemed to summarize the end of the story instead of telling the story. There really may not have been a ton to tell at that point though. I don't want to give away too m uch here. :)<br /><br />I grabbed this book because I found it for less than $1 knowing nothing about it. Just the thought of "Dating Big Bird" was intriguing and very odd. There is no actual Big Bird in the story, just a stuffed one. I wouldn't spend a chunk of change on the book, but it was a fast read that offers a different point of view on a topic that I am so familiar with: motherhood.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/6400542-sheila" class="user" title="Sheila">Sheila</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer564706818">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6234904656609174226">This book was...ok. Not too deep. About a modern woman, Ellen Franck, facing the age old insurmountable problem: how do you find a marriageable husband in order to have a baby? Ellen's biological clock ticks loudly away in her heart, and she takes cues from those around her-her sister her boss, her new friendship with a fellow high school alum, among countless other-on her quest to figure out her path. She has a fabulous job which is wearing on her, and a frozen boyfriend, Malcolm, who cannot se</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6234904656609174226">This book was...ok. Not too deep. About a modern woman, Ellen Franck, facing the age old insurmountable problem: how do you find a marriageable husband in order to have a baby? Ellen's biological clock ticks loudly away in her heart, and she takes cues from those around her-her sister her boss, her new friendship with a fellow high school alum, among countless other-on her quest to figure out her path. She has a fabulous job which is wearing on her, and a frozen boyfriend, Malcolm, who cannot seem to live up to her needs.In the end, Ellen makes a decision for herself, by herself, and everything (of course) falls into place.<br /><br />I liked that this book is an easy read. The plot, while very relatable to many women, is not all that compelling. And every character is really measured against the single-minded concern of our narrator, her interest in having her own child.<br /><br />I did not find Ellen believable as an aunt (who calls up their niece and nephews to revel in what he or she is wearing that day?), I found her family relationship weird, her single mindedness, weird, and frankly, a little boring...And really? Demi Moore? There are parts which are awfully convenient and contrived.<br /><br />The topic is not one to which I currently relate, but I have related, as I believe every woman has. I also think the way that women constantly measure themselves against others in pursuit of our womanly goals is accurately enough presented. In that reality, it does not make me proud to be a woman.<br />This is the kind of book that makes me feel like I could write a big, and for that, Laura Zigman, I thank you.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_664280592">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/664280592" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10549695-margaret" class="left imgcol" title="Margaret"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1390960671p2/10549695.jpg" alt="Margaret" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/664280592?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 12, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10549695-margaret" class="user" title="Margaret">Margaret</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/136268.Dating_Big_Bird" title="Paperback 9780385333412" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer664280592">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4069792286063567009">Sure, Ellen Franck was excited when her sister became pregnant but she never counted on falling head over heels in love as a result. The minute she held her newborn niece, Nicole (known as Pickle) her heart was stolen and she knew what it was that she was missing in her life. Ellen, 35,hates the term of "biological clock" but she knows that her chances of having a child of her own are diminishing as each day passes. She is in love with a gentle man and has been in a relationship with him for ove</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4069792286063567009">Sure, Ellen Franck was excited when her sister became pregnant but she never counted on falling head over heels in love as a result. The minute she held her newborn niece, Nicole (known as Pickle) her heart was stolen and she knew what it was that she was missing in her life. Ellen, 35,hates the term of "biological clock" but she knows that her chances of having a child of her own are diminishing as each day passes. She is in love with a gentle man and has been in a relationship with him for over a year; but he is broken. Divorced after the death of his son, he lost the ability to be intimate with anyone. He will not risk another love, another child and when Ellen asks him point blank to help her have a child, no strings attached, the relationship crumbles.<br /><br />Ellen ponders and researches and discusses with her friends and her sister her options. She knows to have a child as a single parent would not be easy for her or for her child. Should she follow her heart and go forward with "artificial" means of becoming pregnant? Ellen does not make her final decision lightly and as Ellen becomes informed of the details of artificial insemination and its pros and cons, so does the reader.<br /><br />The title and cover of this book made me think I was going to read a side-splitting, laugh out loud comedy. While I did smile and chuckle, I found the book to be a tender and wistful story of many women like Ellen who, rather than settle for a male partner as a means to an end, want to have a child even if it means going it alone.<br /><br />I loved the characters in this story and how they came to life as people I would enjoy knowing and having as my own friends. But the character who stole my heart, just as she did Ellen's, was Pickle. I don't know Zigman's personal bio, but she certainly knows children...at least toddlers and their ability to drive a person to distraction and at the same time melt your heart and make you laugh at the same time. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4069792286063567009">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9077077301938445998">I was really disappointed with this book. It's about Ellen, a single woman who wants a child. I thought I'd be able to relate to wanting a child so much, but she wants one for all the wrong reasons. Her boyfriend is a jerk, &amp; after she dumps him &amp; makes a fortune designing a stupid necklace for her boss she decided to go to a sperm bank. It's disgusting how they screen the sperm donors so they mostly have blonde, blue-eyed guys over 6 feet tall with above average IQ's &amp; perfect family histories to assure that the clients get "perfect" children. From what I've heard that's how it is in real life too. Also, it was odd that Ellen's 4-year-old niece still talks baby talk &amp; is not potty trained, &amp; no one was worried about that, I dont think the author knew very much about children. And I wont give away the ending but I will say it shows what bad judgement Ellen has &amp; that she probably wont be the best mother.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/664515-patricia" class="user" title="Patricia">Patricia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/664515-patricia?shelf=annoying-books" class="actionLinkLite">annoying-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/664515-patricia?shelf=read-in-2009" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2009</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer67301949">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16230797081335662565">I have no desire to have children and thus, was at a disadvantage with this book. The main character is obsessed with having a child. The fact that she is in a relationship with a man who wants no children, and shows no signs of changing that view, is one of the conundrums of the plot.<br /><br />I couldn't relate to the main character. I found the story annoying. I found the writing style in which the author repeatedly uses:<br />Many very short.<br />Sentences like this.<br />Over and over.<br />Again.<br />to be very distracting. The</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16230797081335662565">I have no desire to have children and thus, was at a disadvantage with this book. The main character is obsessed with having a child. The fact that she is in a relationship with a man who wants no children, and shows no signs of changing that view, is one of the conundrums of the plot.<br /><br />I couldn't relate to the main character. I found the story annoying. I found the writing style in which the author repeatedly uses:<br />Many very short.<br />Sentences like this.<br />Over and over.<br />Again.<br />to be very distracting. The plot point at the end of the book, which is the catalyst for change in the protagonist's life, I found to be entirely unbelievable. Why not just have her win the lottery? And the last chapter? Total cop-out.<br /><br />There was nothing redeeming about this book and only an incredibly lazy day got me to finish this book. I was too lazy to start a new one. Not recommended.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer94482535">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17852220579920465624">Very satisfying read, a quick one too, and often hard to put down. This story is a mixture of wry humor, psychological insight, and dreams of the best possible outcome ever. Like others have said, the ending was a bit too dreamy, too "perfect." My only criticism is that it actually would have been much more satisfying if the ending had been written differently. I liked that this author opened up the door to accepting single motherhood by choice, but then regretted seeing her almost compulsively</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17852220579920465624">Very satisfying read, a quick one too, and often hard to put down. This story is a mixture of wry humor, psychological insight, and dreams of the best possible outcome ever. Like others have said, the ending was a bit too dreamy, too "perfect." My only criticism is that it actually would have been much more satisfying if the ending had been written differently. I liked that this author opened up the door to accepting single motherhood by choice, but then regretted seeing her almost compulsively throw Ellen into a couple RIGHT before the end of the story. Would have loved to see Ellen stay single but hopeful, to see her joyful at her approaching single motherhood while raising the bar for that special someone who may enter her and her child's lives.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17852220579920465624">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2804796715477380525">An uneven novel that doesn't compare to her previous effort, Animal Husbandry. I still think Zigman is one of the more intelligent chick-lit writers around, but it seems she gets a bit lazy with this one. The descriptions of the relationship the main character was in resonated with me more than the whole I-want-a-baby-sooooo-bad stuff, but even so, I was a bit annoyed at how unrealistic things became, particularly towards the end. I will say I was surprised by the ending, but that's just me, onc</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2804796715477380525">An uneven novel that doesn't compare to her previous effort, Animal Husbandry. I still think Zigman is one of the more intelligent chick-lit writers around, but it seems she gets a bit lazy with this one. The descriptions of the relationship the main character was in resonated with me more than the whole I-want-a-baby-sooooo-bad stuff, but even so, I was a bit annoyed at how unrealistic things became, particularly towards the end. I will say I was surprised by the ending, but that's just me, once again, comparing it to Animal Husbandry (much better, imho). So if you want the good beach read, go for that instead.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/289983-candice" class="user" title="Candice">Candice</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/136268.Dating_Big_Bird" title="Paperback 9780385333412" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/289983-candice?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/289983-candice?shelf=chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer4793621">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3274965974020492359">I'd read Animal Husbandry, by this same author, and liked it, so I bought this one when it was on the bargain books aisle at Barnes &amp; Noble. To the extent that I paid $4 for a hardback (which I always love), I liked it okay. The author has some funny, quirky ways she writes things, which I like, and I don't recall too many (any?) other books about a woman wanting to get pregnant via articial insemination, so it gets points for a different topic. The ending is a bit nauseating to me, but they</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3274965974020492359">I'd read Animal Husbandry, by this same author, and liked it, so I bought this one when it was on the bargain books aisle at Barnes &amp; Noble. To the extent that I paid $4 for a hardback (which I always love), I liked it okay. The author has some funny, quirky ways she writes things, which I like, and I don't recall too many (any?) other books about a woman wanting to get pregnant via articial insemination, so it gets points for a different topic. The ending is a bit nauseating to me, but they gotta wrap it up in a nice bow, I guess....I liked Animal Husbandry better than this book, but hey, I got this one cheap.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3274965974020492359">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5984524625618578113">This one was OK. The concept wasn't bad: a mid-30s singelish woman living in NYC really wants to be a mother. Unfortunately, the way the story unfold wasn't that great, and the events didn't always flow smoothly. I think this could have been a much better story if the writing had been more cohesive, and perhaps if it wasn't the story of a woman working in the fashion industry. That made me feel as if the story should have been funnier, since all books with the fashion industry as a "character" h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5984524625618578113">This one was OK. The concept wasn't bad: a mid-30s singelish woman living in NYC really wants to be a mother. Unfortunately, the way the story unfold wasn't that great, and the events didn't always flow smoothly. I think this could have been a much better story if the writing had been more cohesive, and perhaps if it wasn't the story of a woman working in the fashion industry. That made me feel as if the story should have been funnier, since all books with the fashion industry as a "character" have some element of humor to them.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17174218301498418796">While this was an interesting look at the decisions some women face, I really didn't like it in the end. It seemed too easy, too wrapped up in a nice neat ball... And I can say as a sister and mother that I don't think I'd ever give the advice to go it alone when having a child, but maybe that's just me. That said, it's got humor and some interesting character types. Setting up the conflicts was great, very believable, but the climax and resolution left something to be desired. I guess reality m</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ruqtHQobkBgW9inZ7brgL2vP+Hi8+hgbsOfXoYYJnK7LPpLO+MmE4pouXWKT2wadIjg7YfUnX7Ha7tIzSpxq6w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/78787.Laura_Zigman">About Laura Zigman</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/78787.Laura_Zigman"><img alt="78787" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1393598088p2/78787.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer14602595929387231190">Laura Zigman grew up in Newton, Massachusetts, and graduated from the University of Massachusetts at Amherst and the Radcliffe Publishing Procedures Course.<br /><br />She spent ten years working in New York in book publishing where she was a publicist for Times Books, Vintage Books, Turtle Bay Books, Atlantic Monthly Press, and Alfred A. Knopf.<br /><br />After moving to Washington, D.C. and working briefly as a project</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14602595929387231190">Laura Zigman grew up in Newton, Massachusetts, and graduated from the University of Massachusetts at Amherst and the Radcliffe Publishing Procedures Course.<br /><br />She spent ten years working in New York in book publishing where she was a publicist for Times Books, Vintage Books, Turtle Bay Books, Atlantic Monthly Press, and Alfred A. Knopf.<br /><br />After moving to Washington, D.C. and working briefly as a project manager for The Smithsonian Associates and a consultant for Share Our Strength, an anti-poverty non-profit group, she finished her first novel. Animal Husbandry was published in 1998 by The Dial Press and became a national bestseller. It was published in fourteen countries and in 2001 the film based on the book, Someone Like You, starring Ashley Judd and Hugh Jackman, was released by Fox 2000. Her second novel, Dating Big Bird, also published by The Dial Press, came out in 2000, and her third novel, Her, published by Knopf followed in 2002. Her latest novel, Piece of Work, to be published by Warner Books on September 25, 2006 , is based on her experiences as a publicist and has been optioned by Tom Hanks' production company, Playtone Pictures, with My Big Fat Greek Wedding's Nia Vardalos set to write the screenplay and star in the movie .<br /><br />She currently lives outside Boston with her husband and young son<br /><br />Retrieved from "<a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laura_Zigman" target="_blank">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laura_Zi...</a>"<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14602595929387231190">...more</a>

    </div>
